** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Economy,_trade,_and_companies|prev|857284370|ECON 857284370}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Opinions are requested as to whether the numeric colour values (RGB, HSV and Hexadecimal) in the various tables in this article are appropriate? Is this excessively detailed overcoverage? If such values are deemed potentially appropriate, further opinions are requested as to how they can be validly referenced to provide [[WP:V|verifiability]]. It has become clear (from discussion above) that these values were derived from colour swatches and sampled from websites in what I believe to be an act of [[WP:OR|original research]]. I believe the values to be unverified and also intrinsically unverifiable. As a glance at the discussion above will reveal, this is very strongly disputed with no consensus as the correct way to apply the policies, so opinions on this are requested. I have removed the value columns once and have been reverted. Ultimately, '''I would like to know whether to remove them again?''' If there is a consensus to remove them here, should similar columns of values also be removed from any of the other articles in the Crayola walled garden that survive their AfDs? --[[User:DanielRigal|DanielRigal]] ([[User talk:DanielRigal|talk]]) 18:52, 31 July 2018 (UTC)}}

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Religion_and_philosophy|prev|857603855|RELI 857603855}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
There was a tag on this page and [[Baconian method]] to merge this one into that one place in August 2018. I saw an old discussion with no real comment but saw the tag was recent so I went and did it. Hasty sure but bold and it seemed obvious to me that it should be done as the Baconian method is not so much a topic unto itself as one of many things covered in Novum Organum. My work was revert due to no discussion or consensus despite the similarity of the topic. The reverting editor had good point though, Novum Organum ought to be the page that remains if a merger is to occur. So I figured flipping the merger proposal and tagging an RfC would be a good way to drum up some conversation.

Obviously I support a merger since I went ahead and did the work, which can be seen [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baconian_method&oldid=853888843 here]. Although I definitely didn't finish. Also, the new merge would clearly be different then what I did given they would be going together in the opposite direction. I contend that it's basically the same content but on the Baconian method page there is less of it and also some irrelevant stuff.

What do we think would work? I consensus is leave the separate I'll work on a separate improvement of Baconian method or just move on to another project but I'd like to merge them. [[User:Rap Chart Mike|Rap Chart Mike]] ([[User talk:Rap Chart Mike|talk]]) 19:04, 9 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Deletion policy#rfc_77B744B|Wikipedia talk:Deletion policy]] expired 2018-09-02 01:01 ===
* Id: 77B744B
* User: Adam9007
* Date: 2018-08-03 00:18:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|853187172|POLICY 853187172}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|857646866|POLICY 857646866}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I searched the archives of both here and [[WP:VPP]] and couldn't find much, so I apologise if this has been discussed recently. From what I can tell, [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:Deletion_policy&diff=next&oldid=109283992 this] is the beginning of WP:ATD in its present form, and it has remained largely the same ever since, albeit with a few additions and amendments over the years. I don't know if it had consensus, and I see no point in trying to find out, because it won't change anything even if there was consensus: it's the consensus of today that matters, not the consensus of 11 years ago. And I'm not entirely convinced that the community actually agrees with its status as policy: there are many, many cases of what would appear to be [[WP:IGNORINGATD]] cases (which I actually find a bit strange as I was under the impression that [[WP:ATA]] is a widely accepted essay on deletion?).

*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Cad-Capture Group]] - Client of a notable organisation, yet no-one even considered [[WP:ATD-M]] or [[WP:ATD-R]].
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Vergenoegd Primary School]] - A redirect per [[WP:ATD-R]] would still have fixed the problem.
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Tuncay √ñzt√ºrk]] - This was speedied as G7, but that aside, [[WP:ATD-M]] or [[WP:ATD-R]] were likely still applicable (see [[WP:INVALIDBIO]])
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/The Art of Problem Solving]] - Again, redirection would also have solved the problem.
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Lifoti]] - Notable (or so it was thought at the time) founder, but no merge or redirect for whatever reason (it should be noted that the founder's article was later deleted).
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Grace (musical group)]] - Notable member, yet I was the only one who even mentioned an alternative to deletion. Also, despite ATD, [[WP:FAILN]], and even CSD policy itself (which does say ATD applies), my A7 decline on those grounds was "invalid reasoning".
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Joe (website)]] - You could be forgiven for thinking '''''I''''' was in the wrong just by mentioning alternatives! I'll let the AfD and [[User_talk:Adam9007/Archive_2#Notability_is_not_inherited|this "discussion"]] do the rest of the talking.
*[[GF Biochemicals]] - Here we likely had [[WP:ATD-E]] and [[WP:ATD-I]], but even in the worst case scenario, we had [[WP:ATD-R]]. But A7 prevailed per [[WP:NOTINHERITED]]. It was restored, not because it was decided the A7 was wrong, but because someone wanted to improve it. In fact, if memory serves, there was a pretty much unanimous consensus that it indeed ''should'' have been speedied under A7.  If I remember right, [[WP:ATD]] occurred to no-one (myself included if I'm not mistaken!). 
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Data Networking/Spring 2017/]] - [[WP:ATD-TRANS]] was obvious, but nope.
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Camp Camp]] - While this ''was'' redirected, from what I can tell it was entirely at the closer's discretion. Consensus was to delete and no alternative was considered.
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Ajit Gunewardene (2nd nomination)]] - No redirect, going against [[WP:ATD-R]] and [[WP:INVALIDBIO]].
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Xtian de Medici]] - {{tquote|The topic is already covered in [[Gunner_de_Medici]]}}. So why not redirect there?
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Deep Eddy Vodka Distillery]] - {{tquote|the Heaven Hill article already mentions the brand}}. {{tquote|The parent article already mentions it}}. Same as above.
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Levi Sanders]] - Could have been redirected to his notable parent, but that wasn't talked about (another target was proposed, but that wasn't to be either).
*[[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Hurricane (group)]] - Apparently had a notable member, but wasn't merged or redirected.

There are likely many more out there (i do remember articles having merge/redirect targets getting speedied under A7, but can't remember what they were). I also noticed that an admin said [[Wikipedia:Village_pump_(policy)/Archive_140#Pruning/blanking_abandoned_very_bad_articles|here]] that many editors ignore ATD entirely, and I have to concur. I have to question [[WP:ATD]]'s status as policy, if it's ignored so easily so often. I can think of no other policy where you can easily get away with pretending it doesn't exist. ATD may be a good principle, but from what I can see it's far from a "widely accepted standard that all editors should normally follow". Policy is supposed to reflect the norm. not dictate it, no? Thoughts? [[User:Adam9007|Adam9007]] ([[User talk:Adam9007|talk]]) 00:18, 3 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Naming conventions (geographic names)#rfc_74DD98D|Wikipedia talk:Naming conventions (geographic names)]] expired 2018-09-02 10:01 ===
* Id: 74DD98D
* User: Jamacfarlane
* Date: 2018-08-03 09:46:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|853237496|STYLE 853237496}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|857685637|STYLE 857685637}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
'''Should schools be disambiguated in the form "Name High School, Town" or "Name High School (Town)"?'''
My preference is to use a single comma, but two editors have commented this style is improper (without pointing to anywhere in the guidelines). A school doesn't fit well into either [[WP:NCCORP]] or [[WP:NCPLACE]]. In my view, a single comma is the most natural way to disambiguate, and in any case using brackets is grammatically incorrect (strictly it should be "Name High School (high school in Town)").
[[User:Jamacfarlane|jamacfarlane]] ([[User talk:Jamacfarlane|talk]]) 09:46, 3 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Reliable sources/Noticeboard#rfc_3C6FBBF|Wikipedia:Reliable sources/Noticeboard]] expired 2018-09-02 14:01 ===
* Id: 3C6FBBF
* Date: 2018-09-02 12:40:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|857701849|POL 857701849}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|861137813|POL 861137813}}
* RFC Text:

Politifact rates most checked claims by Occupy Democrats as false and very few as unambiguously true: [https://www.politifact.com/personalities/occupy-democrats/]. Should Occupy Democrats be deprecated as a source in the same was as [[WP:DAILYMAIL]] and other partisan sites with a poor reputation for factual accuracy? 
'''Opinions'''
* '''Support''' as nominator. "Our mission is to Occupy Democrats on November 2018 AND BEYOND by voting in a LANDSLIDE of progressive Democratic candidates dedicated to rolling back President Trump‚Äôs extremist agenda." This is my aim too, but it does not mark them out as a reliable source for anything. It's a political activist movement, not even a formally constituted political party, and there is little or no accountability for what is said in Occupy's name or  Most links are now removed (by me and others, over a long period), and few of these removals have been challenged. It's my view that we should not source anything to Occupy other than strictly factual and uncontroversial facts about Occupy on the articles related to Occupy and related people - if a claim is not covered in more reliable sources then it's not significant and probably [[WP:UNDUE]], if it is, we should use them instead. <b>[[User Talk:JzG|Guy]]</b> <small>([[User:JzG/help|Help!]])</small> 12:40, 2 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Pennsylvania's 7th and 15th congressional district special elections, 2018#rfc_7F1897A|Talk:Pennsylvania's 7th and 15th congressional district special elections, 2018]] expired 2018-09-05 01:01 ===
* Id: 7F1897A
* User: Nevermore27
* Date: 2018-08-06 00:30:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|853625386|POL 853625386}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|858094282|POL 858094282}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Before last night no dedicated article existed for the two PA congressional special elections that will be taking place this November. I created this one last night, and decided to create a single article for both elections. Here are my reasons for doing so
#I can't remember the last time two congressional special elections took place in the same state on the same day, so had no precedent to go off of.
#The elections are being held under the 2011 PA map which was invalidated by ''LWV v. PA'', meaning that the districts will functionally cease to exist the moment the election is certified.
#In addition, these are elections to the [[Lame-duck session]] of the [[115th United States Congress]], so the winners of these special elections will be serving their districts for a maximum of 2 months, lowering the stakes of these particular elections.
#The nominees for both parties are the same as the successor districts for the regular 2018 elections.

So: '''keep''' merged or '''separate'''? I welcome your comments. '''[[User:Nevermore27|<span style="color: #660198">Nevermore27</span>]]''' ([[User talk:Nevermore27|talk]]) 00:30, 6 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Trans woman#rfc_92B3D94|Talk:Trans woman]] expired 2018-09-05 22:01 ===
* Id: 92B3D94
* User: DIYeditor

* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Language_and_linguistics|prev|853770025|LANG 853770025}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|853770029|POL 853770029}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|853770034|SOC 853770034}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Language_and_linguistics|prev|858241059|LANG 858241059}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|858241063|POL 858241063}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|858241066|SOC 858241066}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
There has been extensive discussion at [[Wikipedia:Neutral point of view/Noticeboard]] as to whether the current introductory sentence of [[Trans woman]] is appropriate. From the discussion come these proposals <ins>for the introductory sentence</ins>:

# A '''trans woman''' (sometimes '''trans-woman''' or '''transwoman''') is a [[woman]] who was [[assigned male at birth]].
# A '''trans woman''' (sometimes '''trans-woman''' or '''transwoman''') is a person who was [[sex assignment|assigned male at birth]] but [[gender identity|identifies as a woman]].
# A '''trans woman''' (sometimes '''trans-woman''' or '''transwoman''') is a woman whose [[biological sex]] does not align with their [[gender identity]].
# A '''trans woman''' (sometimes '''trans-woman''' or '''transwoman''') is a male-to-female (MTF) [[transsexual]] or [[transgender]] person.
# General support for describing a trans woman as a woman.
# General support for describing a trans woman as a person.
# General support for "assigned".
# General support for "biological".

Although it may complicate things slightly for the closer, feel free to combine multiple options. [[User:DIYeditor|‚ÄîDIYeditor]] ([[User talk:DIYeditor|talk]]) 21:07, 6 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:List of people who disappeared mysteriously#rfc_E87803A|Talk:List of people who disappeared mysteriously]] expired 2018-09-06 04:01 ===
* Id: E87803A
* User: GreenC
* Date: 2018-09-06 01:45:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|858275980|SOC 858275980}}
* RFC Text:

Should the talk pages for [[Talk:List of people who disappeared mysteriously: pre-1970]] and [[Talk:List of people who disappeared mysteriously: post-1970]] redirect here so there is a single talk page? Or should each they have their own talk pages?

'''Survey'''

*'''Support''' single page (nom). This article was recently broken into two sections for technical limitations, it was too large for some users overseas who were unable to load it. This was a 'necessary evil' as ideally the list would remain intact. So it was suggested that we at least keep the talk page centralized as discussions here generally impact both articles, keeping discussions central to the list as a whole avoids forking of similar discussions such as inclusion criteria. However, these talk redirects have been opposed by editors trying to impliment article assessment templates ([https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Talk%3AList_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously%3A_pre-1970&type=revision&diff=858218825&oldid=858214945 example]). Thus this RfC to decide what is wanted, three talk pages or one.  -- [[User:GreenC|<span style="color: #006A4E;">'''Green'''</span>]][[User talk:GreenC|<span style="color: #093;">'''C'''</span>]] 01:45, 6 September 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
A lot of the mountains at [[:Category:Mountains of Oppland]] are stubs with little or no facts beyond their stats.  I have checked a couple of them and their sources may not satisfy [[WP:GEOLAND]], which states that

{{cquote|Named natural features are often notable, '''provided information beyond statistics and coordinates is known to exist.''' This includes mountains, lakes, streams, islands, etc. '''The number of known sources should be considered to ensure there is enough verifiable content for an encyclopedic article.''' If a Wikipedia article cannot be developed using known sources, information on the feature can instead be included in a more general article on local geography. '''For example, a river island with no information available except name and location should probably be described in an article on the river.'''}} 

While the mountains might be named, it would fail that criteria because of the bolded parts.  Do you think we should combine the mountains into one article (ie merge them) as {{u|Power~enwiki}} suggests at [[Wikipedia:Articles for deletion/Vestre Hestl√¶gerh√∏y]]. === [[Wikipedia talk:Interface administrators#rfc_8C91165|Wikipedia talk:Interface administrators]] expired 2018-09-07 10:01 ===
* Id: 8C91165
* User: Mz7
* Date: 2018-09-02 00:51:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|857635157|PROP 857635157}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|857652134|POLICY 857652134}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|857760544|TECH 857760544}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|858457824|POLICY 858457824}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|858457826|TECH 858457826}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|858457831|PROP 858457831}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Should we adopt the following process regarding the interface administrator permission?
{{ivmbox|1=<nowiki />
; Process for requesting
Administrators who wish to request this permission may make a new request at [[Wikipedia:Interface administrators' noticeboard]] ([[WP:IANB]]). A notice should be posted to [[WP:VPT]] and [[WP:AN]] to invite community participation. Those making a request are encouraged to answer the following two questions:

* Please describe any relevant on-wiki experience you have for this role.
* Please outline, without breaching your personal privacy, any off-wiki experience or technical expertise you may have for this role.

Requests will be open for one week, during which any editor may comment on the request. Editors are encouraged to comment on the requester's level of trust and technical ability. Requests will be closed by a [[WP:bureaucrat|bureaucrat]].

; Removal of permissions
Permission should be removed by bureaucrats in the following circumstances:
#Interface administrators who have made no edits or other logged action for at least 12 months should have the user right removed.
#Voluntary request by the interface administrator at the [[Wikipedia:Bureaucrats' noticeboard| bureaucrats' noticeboard]].
#After misuse of the access, by consensus at [[Wikipedia:Administrators' noticeboard]].
#Upon removal of administrator access, for any reason.
#By request of the [[Wikipedia:Arbitration Committee|Arbitration Committee]].
}}
To be clear, this is the text that is [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:Interface_administrators&oldid=857630229 currently] on the main [[Wikipedia:Interface administrators]] page, authored primarily by {{U|Enterprisey}} in the section "[[Wikipedia talk:Interface administrators#Yet another proposed granting process|Yet another proposed granting process]]" above. [[User:Mz7|Mz7]] ([[User talk:Mz7|talk]]) 00:51, 2 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Blocking policy#rfc_0C1E238|Wikipedia talk:Blocking policy]] expired 2018-09-07 12:01 ===
* Id: 0C1E238
* Date: 2018-09-04 16:02:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|858033063|POLICY 858033063}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|858033067|PROP 858033067}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|858468713|POLICY 858468713}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|858468715|PROP 858468715}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Should the following be adopted in regards to blocked users editing their talk pages?
;[[Wikipedia:Blocking policy]] ([[WP:OPTIONS]])
;:Current text
{{ivmbox|bg=#f8f9fa|1=<nowiki />
* '''Prevent this user from editing their own talk page while blocked''', if checked, will prevent the blocked user from editing their own talk page (including the ability to create unblock requests) during the duration of their block. This option is not checked by default, and typically should '''not''' be checked; editing of the user's talk page should be disabled only in the case of continued abuse of their user talk page. The [[Wikipedia:Protection policy#Blocked users|protection policy]] has further details in cases where ''other users'' are repeatedly causing disruption to the user talk pages of blocked users.
}}
;:Proposed text #1 (All blocked editors)
{{ivmbox|1=<nowiki />
* '''Prevent this user from editing their own talk page while blocked''', if checked, will prevent the blocked user from editing their own talk page (including the ability to create unblock requests) during the duration of their block. This option is not checked by default, and typically should '''not''' be checked; editing of the user's talk page should be disabled only in the case of continued abuse of their user talk page<ins>, including any blocked user editing their talk page for anything other than a block appeal</ins>. The [[Wikipedia:Protection policy#Blocked users|protection policy]] has further details in cases where ''other users'' are repeatedly causing disruption to the user talk pages of blocked users.
}}
;:Proposed text #2 (Indefinitely blocked editors)
{{ivmbox|1=<nowiki />
* '''Prevent this user from editing their own talk page while blocked''', if checked, will prevent the blocked user from editing their own talk page (including the ability to create unblock requests) during the duration of their block. This option is not checked by default, and typically should '''not''' be checked; editing of the user's talk page should be disabled only in the case of continued abuse of their user talk page<ins>, including any indefinitely blocked user editing their talk page for anything other than a block appeal</ins>. The [[Wikipedia:Protection policy#Blocked users|protection policy]] has further details in cases where ''other users'' are repeatedly causing disruption to the user talk pages of blocked users.
}}

The difference between the two is that '''Proposed text #1''' is for all blocked users, while '''Proposed text #2''' is for all indefinitely blocked users. 

This proposal stems from the lengthy and divisive discussion at [[Wikipedia:Administrators%27_noticeboard/IncidentArchive991#Improper_use_of_talk_page_while_blocked|ANI]]. Please read through that discussion before commenting or voting here. Additionally, please comment on whether you support one version, both versions and the order you support them, or oppose to proposal entirely. [[User:Nihlus|<span style="padding:2px 2px;font-variant:small-caps;color:#000;letter-spacing:-0.5px">'''Nihlus'''</span>]] 16:02, 4 September 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=

<blockquote>In 1869, a new [[Presidency of Ulysses S. Grant#Indian affairs and human rights|Peace Policy]] nominally promised to protect Native-Americans from abuses, avoid further war, and secure their eventual U.S. citizenship. Nonetheless, conflicts and state-sanctioned murder, including the [[California Genocide]], continued throughout the West into the 1900s.<ref> Madley, Benjamin (2016). ''An American Genocide: The United States and the California Indian Catastrophe, 1846-1873.'' Yale University Press. ‚Äîin replacement of the text currently there:<blockquote>In 1869, a new [[Presidency of Ulysses S. Grant#Indian affairs and human rights|Peace Policy]] sought to protect Native-Americans from abuses, avoid further war, and secure their eventual U.S. citizenship, although conflicts, including several of the largest Indian Wars, continued throughout the West into the 1900s.<ref name=Smith_pp525-526>Smith (2001), ''Grant'', pp. 523‚Äì526</ref></blockquote>

=== [[Talk:Lisa Littman#rfc_909AEB7|Talk:Lisa Littman]] expired 2018-09-11 07:01 ===

* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|858970305|UNSORTED 858970305}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|859026670|UNSORTED 859026670}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
At this time, I think the article is adequately [[WP:NPOV|NPOV]]-compliant on the topic of ROGD. However, it is clearly {{em|not}} NPOV-compliant on the topic of [[Lisa Littman]], the nominal subject of the page. It's still a [[WP:BLP|BLP]] that has instead become a [[WP:coatrack|coatrack]] for a [[WP:RECENT]] controversy, resulting in serious issues including [[WP:BALASP]].

Despite legitimate concerns about [[WP:RECENT|recentism]] and [[WP:NOTNEWS]], I think we have a consensus that the ROGD content of this article belongs in Wikipedia, {{em|somewhere}}. But there's no consensus about what action should be taken.

These are the possibilities that I see, and I'm inviting a discussion under each heading.

''' Promptly delete the entire BLP '''

Delete the entire article on [[Lisa Littman]], based on [[WP:BLP1E]] and lack of notability under [[WP:PROF]]:
* '''Oppose''': The subject is currently at least [[WP:NOTABLE]] enough to have a stub or start-class article. <small><span style="color:#0;border:0;font-weight:normal;padding:0 1px 0 1px;text-shadow:1px 4px 8px #F70,-8px -6px 10px #ee7f2d,1px 1px 1px #FFF;">[[User:Lwarrenwiki|Lwarrenwiki]] ([[User talk:Lwarrenwiki|talk]])</span></small> 19:46, 7 September 2018 (UTC)}}

* Date: 2018-08-13 03:56:00

{{rfcquote|text=
I'm asking this [[User talk:Molecule Extraction#Pakatan Harapan colors: Is it red or light blue?|on behalf of the user who asking me in my talkpage]] regarding the colour that was used by the [[Pakatan Harapan]] (PH) coalition in the recent election. While it is acknowledged that the red colour (#C63B38 colour pattern) has been part of the colour symbol of PH coalition, the coalition [https://sg.news.yahoo.com/finally-pakatan-harapan-gets-registered-105315110.html was recently legalised when they won the 9 May election] with the colour began to be used officially. During the election, each parties in the coalition contesting using the flag of [[People's Justice Party (Malaysia)|People's Justice Party]] (PKR) with blue colour (#00ADEF colour pattern) for West Malaysia, while in East Malaysia each parties are free to use their respective flags with their own party colours. Both {{U|BrundtBank}} and {{U|Lazybugger13A}} agreed that the main colour that should be used for the entire election articles for [[WP:CONSISTENCY|consistency]] are the red one while {{U|*angys*}} disagreed with the decision as during the election, the coalition was not legalised yet with the parties in West Malaysia contesting under the PKR banner with the blue colour pattern. Due to this endless dispute, I'm inviting other editors especially those who spend their entire time here editing political related articles to find a final [[WP:CONSENSUS|consensus]] on this issue. Regards. [[User:Molecule Extraction|Molecule Extraction]] ([[User talk:Molecule Extraction|talk]]) 03:56, 13 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Signatures#rfc_F6F0FDB|Wikipedia talk:Signatures]] expired 2018-09-12 21:01 ===
* Id: F6F0FDB
* Date: 2018-09-12 18:56:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|859244587|STYLE 859244587}}

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|859244590|PROP 859244590}}
* RFC Text:

Simple question. <span style="background:red; color:yellow; padding:3px;">should</span><span style="background:blue;color:white; padding:3px;">we </span><span style="background:darkslategray;color:pink; padding:3px;">disallow </span><span style="background:green;color:orange; padding:3px;">text </span><span style="background:blue;color:white; padding:3px;">highlighting </span><span style="background:orange;color:brown; padding:3px;">in </span><span style="background:blue;color:yellow; padding:3px;">signatures?</span>

'''Discussion'''

*'''Yes''' - I've long wondered why we don't disallow highlighting in signatures. I get wanting flexibility for users to express themselves in different ways (obviously, I use some custom formatting in my own), and I would say that using different colors for the text seems reasonable. Using text highlighting does not. I find highlighted text incredible distracting to the point I have trouble focusing on the discussion as a whole, and trouble seeing the signatures of other participants. I suspect I'm not alone in that. We should not let signatures pull eyeballs from the substance of the discussion to draw focus on a single user's name. I've thought about proposing this RfC several times in the past, but looking at [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia_talk:Categories,_lists,_and_navigation_templates&oldid=859237467 this page] just now reminded me of how awful the effect is to my concentration. I imagine I'm not alone, but I suppose it's possible. (Sorry to {{u|woodensuperman}}, with whom I have no quarrel, but whose signature is the one I'm talking about on that page. It's not the most egregious I've ever seen, but all I see are woodensuperman billboards all over the page). &mdash; <samp>[[User:Rhododendrites|<span style="font-size:90%;letter-spacing:1px;text-shadow:0px -1px 0px Indigo;">Rhododendrites</span>]] <sup style="font-size:80%;">[[User_talk:Rhododendrites|talk]]</sup></samp> \\ 18:56, 12 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Suicide#rfc_9B25102|Talk:Suicide]] expired 2018-09-12 22:01 ===
* Id: 9B25102
* Date: 2018-08-31 04:07:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|857773844|STYLE 857773844}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|859265664|STYLE 859265664}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The article is written like a textbook on how to eradicate '''Suicide''' from a society, which is at the least offensive and at the most frightening to any who believe in a fundamental inalienable [[right to die]]. Having read [[WP:Offensive]], [[WP:IAR]] would apply for the sake of allowing others to form their own moral opinions, even if neutrality wasn't already a rule. Due-weight doesn't apply here, because no where in [[WP:NPOV]] have wikipedians collectively decided wikipedia's editorial voice should associate moral imperatives belonging to the predominant point-of-view with rigorously cited consensus and [[MOS:Alleged]] facts by how they are told--often by clumping facts useful one particular goal or another next to each other especially in the lede--even if that point-of-view as well as its moral imperatives are enforced by law in many reputable countries. Wikipedians wouldn't hypothetically allow Chinese officials write a communism article that clumps facts useful to writing communist law in the lede, why should suicide be any different?

The medical infobox also carries significant bias (like if an invented "eugenics" infobox plagued articles about ethnicities), though there isn't really a suitable substitute. I would say whatever infobox eventually appears on [[Fetishism]] would do, however in the meanwhile perhaps no infobox or [[Template:Infobox performing art]] instead?

If you disagree, please leave the banner up for at least a week or so to invited discussion from non-wikipedians. <s>I'm IP-editing</s> so I won't get notifications about this article and I don't want to get too emotionally invested. 04:07, 31 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Sofia Airport#rfc_B8E0458|Talk:Sofia Airport]] expired 2018-09-13 06:01 ===
* Id: B8E0458
* User: Tdunsky
* Date: 2018-08-14 05:46:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|854847989|POLICY 854847989}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|859310594|POLICY 859310594}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Hello fellow Wikipedians,

We have an ensuing edit war in this article ([[Sofia Airport]]) which I would like your help in resolving. As a result you can also help clarify Wikipedia general policy on the matter.

I, and other users, claim that future routes in an article about an airport or airline - when properly referenced by an independent source e.g. an article in a neutral news site - is valid encyclopedic information. It is in fact common practice in airport articles across Wikipedia. As a result, we have been adding such information to this and other articles.

One other user claims the opposite, that all future route information is unencyclopedic and constitutes advertising and promotional information. As a result that user has been deleting all such information from this article, even when referenced to an independent source, and intends to do that in articles of other airports as well.

You can check out the history of the page for more details.

Your comments and clarifications are welcome. [[User:Tdunsky|Tdunsky]] ([[User talk:Tdunsky|talk]]) 05:46, 14 August 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
How should this article handle the 2011 rapes (if at all)?

'''Option 1)''' Include the following material, in a subsection ("2011 rapes") of the History section:
{{Quote box|quote = In 2011, 19 suspects were arrested for repeated gang rapes of an 11-year-old girl after identification from cell phone video they recorded of one incident.<ref name="apcourt">{{cite news| url=http://www.cbsnews.com/8301-504083_162-20050743-504083.html | work=CBS News | author=Edecio Martinez | title=Cleveland, Texas gang rape suspects appear in court | date=April 5, 2011}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.nytimes.com/2011/03/09/us/09assault.html?_r=1&hp |title=Vicious Assault Shakes Texas Town |author=James C. McKinley Jr. |date=March 8, 2011 |work=New York Times |accessdate=March 10, 2011}}</ref> It was suspected that more may have been involved.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.latimes.com/ktla-gang-rape-texas-girl,0,2243171.story |title=Gang Rape of 11-year-old Girl Recorded on Cell Phones |author= |date=March 9, 2011 |work=Los Angeles Times |accessdate=March 10, 2011}}</ref> The incident, which was reported in the national media, caused much consternation and division in the town. Brisbane|date=11 March 2011|work=The New York Times}}</ref> and the Times subsequently published a clarification.}}

{{Quote box|quote = Ultimately, 21 persons were charged in the case. Two suspects requested jury trials. They were found guilty and sentenced to life in prison (in one case) and 99 years in prison (in the other). === [[Talk:Gender identity#rfc_48259FB|Talk:Gender identity]] expired 2018-09-19 02:01 ===
* Id: 48259FB
* User: Dmezh
* Date: 2018-08-20 01:13:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|855677868|SOC 855677868}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|860205838|SOC 860205838}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The use of the phrase "assigned at birth" and "assigned sex" is redundant and implies that there can be a different '''sex''' from the one a person is born with. Bypassing any opinions on "gender" as it is used in this article, it is biologically impossible to change one's '''sex'''. There is a [[Sex and gender distinction|WP article]] on this distinction (again, I am writing this in terms of the current WP world and do not intend to make a political/moral statement about this topic). 

I move and RfC that the statements containing these phrases should be reworded to reflect definition and the intended wikivoice here. An example:

::"Different amounts of these male or female sex hormones within a person can result in behavior and external genitalia that do not match up with the norm of their sex assigned at birth."

::To: "Different amounts of these male or female sex hormones within a person can result in behavior and external genitalia that do not match up with the normal attributes of their sex."

Again, even the [[Assigned sex|WP article on assigned sex]] is about the determination of a person's sex, and this sex cannot change. Gender is a separate beast here. I do think that perhaps for wikilinking purposes, it can be included once in the article, but it makes no sense to me to have it repeated in this fashion over and over, especially given that it could confuse the uninitiated reader about the accepted distinction between gender and sex.

- [[User:Dmezh|Dmezh]] ([[User talk:Dmezh|talk]]) 01:13, 20 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Hip hop music#rfc_6571826|Talk:Hip hop music]] expired 2018-09-19 07:02 ===
* Id: 6571826
* User: Dmezh
* Date: 2018-08-20 06:13:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|855701977|MEDIA 855701977}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|855701979|SOC 855701979}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|860229429|MEDIA 860229429}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|860229430|SOC 860229430}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This article is long and has a large focus on the history of hip-hop music. As articles are meant to be encyclopedic, this content is too dense and it may be worth looking into splitting some of it off into a new article (e.g. "Origins of hip hop music" or "History of hip hop music").

It is helpful to put yourself into the shoes of the average viewer. I would wager to guess that someone looking for an encyclopedic article on hip hop music ''''might'''' not want to read 20,000 words on the intricate and detailed history of the genre. This article needs generalization.

Let's RfC on a possible future preparation and move-rename of this page to "History of hip hop music" and linked creation of a new "Hip hop music" article. This would take a while, of course. Let me know what you think. - [[User:Dmezh|Dmezh]] ([[User talk:Dmezh|talk]]) 06:13, 20 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_04391CF|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2018-09-25 02:01 ===
* Id: 04391CF
* User: Alpha3031
* Date: 2018-09-03 03:20:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|857805191|POLICY 857805191}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|861095140|POLICY 861095140}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This RfC is a followup to [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)/Archive 135#The criteria of WP:NSPORT here are too inclusive|a June 2017 RfC]] clarifying the relation between SNGs and the GNG. Consensus was established that SNGs do not supersede GNG, but there was no consensus as to what to do about the articles not apparently meeting GNG. [[Wikipedia:Village pump (idea lab)#What to do for stub articles meeting WP:NSPORT but failing WP:GNG?|A pre-RfC discussion]] has show two major issues: What the final result should be, and what to do in the interim to avoid flooding AfD and related venues, which will be discussed as a follow up. The main options are '''keep''', '''tag''', '''merge''', '''transwiki''' or '''delete'''.{{hping|Smartyllama|Johnpacklambert|Nosebagbear|power~enwiki|Masem|Finnusertop|Jayron32|Eastmain|Red Phoenix|Redditaddict69|PohranicniStraze|Kpgjhpjm|Ross-c|Northamerica1000|Knightrises10|Pelmeen10|Jacknstock|GiantSnowman|Groovy|Mattythewhite|Pharaoh of the Wizards|Editorofthewiki|Ifnord|White Shadows}}‚Äî‚Ää[[User:Alpha3031|Alpha3031]] ([[User talk:Alpha3031|t]] ‚Ä¢ [[Special:Contributions/Alpha3031|c]]) 03:20, 3 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Module talk:Infobox military conflict#rfc_74006B5|Module talk:Infobox military conflict]] expired 2018-09-27 04:01 ===
* Id: 74006B5
* User: EtherealGate
* Date: 2018-08-28 03:28:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|856885497|HIST 856885497}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|861399802|HIST 861399802}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
(moved from [[Talk:Battle of the Coral Sea#Request for comment]])

Should infoboxes follow a strict interpretation of [[Template:Infobox military conflict/doc]]? Per the discussion above, articles like [[Wars of the Roses]], [[World War II]], [[World War I]], [[Hundred Years' War]], as well as [[War of the Austrian Succession]], [[King George's War]], [[War of the Spanish Succession]], [[Samoan Civil War]], and many more others are violations. Per the discussion with [[User:Cinderella157|Cinderella157]] above, we cannot use results like "stalemate", "indecisive", "withdrawal", "status quo ante bellum", "ceasefire", "truce", "compromise", simple "treaty" results, or any other description and bullet points as they are contrary of Template:Infobox military conflict/doc. [[User:EtherealGate|EtherealGate]] ([[User talk:EtherealGate|talk]]) 03:28, 28 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Template talk:Iobdb name#rfc_48BFE02|Template talk:Iobdb name]] expired 2018-09-28 04:01 ===
* Id: 48BFE02
* User: Clarkcj12
* Date: 2018-08-29 03:42:00

** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|857034573|TECH 857034573}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_technical_issues_and_templates|prev|861534621|TECH 861534621}}

{{rfcquote|text=
I would like to request an rfc on whether to update the template to pull in Wikdiata information. I do that their was an ArbCom notice back in November of last year about establishing need for it. I would like to suggest that this template be updated to use and pull the Wikidata information, such as the identifier id for it. While some may say why rely on Wikidata, while we should not you need to realize that most of our infobox's pull stuff from Wikidata especially those on our other language versions of Wikipedia, as that is why that project was founded as a catalog of information to make putting information into templates and connecting pages across the language spectrum easier. We don't need to update the template to only pull information from Wikidata but of course allow still the usage of putting the identifier id in manually. Some may think that opens it up to cross project vandalism, well maybe so but Wikidata does have active editors and admins that maintain it. --[[User:Clarkcj12|Clarkcj12]] ([[User talk:Clarkcj12|talk]]) 03:42, 29 August 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Egypt national football team#rfc_2953F2B|Talk:Egypt national football team]] expired 2018-09-28 07:01 ===
* Id: 2953F2B
* User: Ben5218
* Date: 2018-09-03 21:52:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Religion_and_philosophy|prev|857919386|RELI 857919386}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|857919388|SOC 857919388}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Religion_and_philosophy|prev|861547316|RELI 861547316}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|861547317|SOC 861547317}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Christians comprise about 10-20% of Egypt's population, the majority of which are [[Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria|Coptic Orthodox Christians]]<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/view/the-copts-and-their-political-implications-in-egypt|title=The Copts and Their Political Implications in Egypt|website=www.washingtoninstitute.org|language=en|access-date=2018-07-23}}</ref>. However, there is not a single Christian on any of the league's 540 roster spots, or the [[Egypt national football team|national team]]. This disparity is believed to be due to the bias against accepting young talented Christian players at the clubs' youth level throughout the national<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2016/12/egypt-copts-muslim-christian-isis/511007/|title=The Actual War on Christians|last=Tadros|first=Samuel|date=2016-12-17|work=The Atlantic|access-date=2018-07-23|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.albawabhnews.com/1900820|title=ÿßŸÑŸÖŸáŸÜ ÿßŸÑŸÖÿ≠ÿ±ŸÖÿ© ÿπŸÑŸâ ÿßŸÑÿ£ŸÇÿ®ÿßÿ∑|work=ÿßŸÑÿ®Ÿàÿßÿ®ÿ© ŸÜŸäŸàÿ≤|access-date=2018-07-23}}</ref>. 

There have been complaints from the pro Christian group Coptic Solidarity filed to [[FIFA]] regarding the purposeful exclusion of Christians from the league, as well as their exclusion from Egypt's national team. A similar complaint was filled by Coptic Solidarity to the [[International Olympic Committee|International Olympics Committee]] regarding the similar exclusion of Christians on [[Egypt at the Olympics|Egypt's Olympic teams]]. The exclusions are cited as being systemic [[Persecution of Copts|persecution against the Coptic Christians]]. Neither FIFA nor the IOC has taken action or conducted independent research to investigate these complaints<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.standardnewswire.com/news/7391714099.html|title=Coptic Solidarity Urges FIFA to Investigate Discrimination Against Coptic Footballers in Egypt - Standard Newswire|website=www.standardnewswire.com|access-date=2018-07-23}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/coptic-solidarity-files-complaints-with-the-ioc-and-fifa-regarding-egypts-religious-discrimination-against-copts-in-athletics-300317196.html|title=Coptic Solidarity Files Complaints with the IOC and FIFA Regarding Egypt's Religious Discrimination Against Copts in Athletics|website=www.prnewswire.com|language=en|access-date=2018-07-23}}</ref>.

''I believe that the content content that [[User:Sllabib|Sllabib]] is trying to add to the article shouldn't be added to the article not because it's only wrong, but I believe that things like that should be included in the article. Both of us discussed this problem on [[User talk:Ben5218|my talk page]], and despite I gave many examples that proves that there is no religion discrimination in Egypt, we didn't reach anything. So I think more opinions should be heard about this case. [[User:Ben5218|Ben5218]] ([[User talk:Ben5218|talk]]) 21:52, 3 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Suicide#rfc_C42420C|Talk:Suicide]] expired 2018-09-30 05:01 ===
* Id: C42420C
* Date: 2018-08-31 04:07:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|859265662|SOC 859265662}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|860503005|STYLE 860503005}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Maths,_science,_and_technology|prev|861808785|SCI 861808785}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Society,_sports,_and_culture|prev|861808788|SOC 861808788}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|861808792|STYLE 861808792}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The article is written like a textbook on how to eradicate '''Suicide''' from a society, which is at the least offensive and at the most frightening to any who believe in a fundamental inalienable [[right to die]]. Having read [[WP:Offensive]], [[WP:IAR]] would apply for the sake of allowing others to form their own moral opinions, even if neutrality wasn't already a rule. Due-weight doesn't apply here, because no where in [[WP:NPOV]] have wikipedians collectively decided wikipedia's editorial voice should associate moral imperatives belonging to the predominant point-of-view with rigorously cited consensus and [[MOS:Alleged]] facts by how they are told--often by clumping facts useful one particular goal or another next to each other especially in the lede--even if that point-of-view as well as its moral imperatives are enforced by law in many reputable countries. Wikipedians wouldn't hypothetically allow Chinese officials write a communism article that clumps facts useful to writing communist law in the lede, why should suicide be any different?

The medical infobox also carries significant bias (like if an invented "eugenics" infobox plagued articles about ethnicities), though there isn't really a suitable substitute. I would say whatever infobox eventually appears on [[Fetishism]] would do, however in the meanwhile perhaps no infobox or [[Template:Infobox performing art]] instead?

If you disagree, please leave the banner up for at least a week or so to invited discussion from non-wikipedians. <s>I'm IP-editing</s> so I won't get notifications about this article and I don't want to get too emotionally invested. 04:07, 31 August 2018 (UTC)}}

"We don't debate Truth, and we definitely do not deal with "hard evidence". Truth and evidence count for almost nothing under Wikipedia policies and decision making processes. We summarize what [[WP:RS|Reliable Sources]] say. If all of the sources said the moon was made of green cheese, then we would ''accurately'' summarize what those sources say. We limit the use of [[WP:primary|primary]] sources such as tax forms. In particular it would be a violation of policy [[WP:SYNTH|SYNTH]] to use tax forms to support this kind of claim. We mainly rely on secondary sources. The existing Newyorker reference is fine. It's a reputable source for news and information, and we can report what they say. If there were contradictory sources then we would have something to sort out. A new source with more specific info would be nice, but not necessary.[[User:Alsee|Alsee]] ([[User talk:Alsee|talk]]) 18:46, 30 September 2018 (UTC)}}

Per {{reply to|Only in death}}'s request, I have formally included a request for comments regarding Lori Maddox's inclusion in this article. The reasons I give are listed in the above "Lori Maddox" section. To summarize them briefly, his involvement with her is well-documented. For the reasons above, I have created this request for comments to answer the following question: **Should Lori Maddox be mentioned in the article?** (We can leave the "how" to a later discussion IF the consensus here is "yes." For now, I just want to see if there is a consensus that she SHOULD be included). Obviously my vote is "yes." [[User:Et0048|Et0048]] ([[User talk:Et0048|talk]]) 19:44, 5 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Shortcut#rfc_97F9521|Wikipedia talk:Shortcut]] expired 2018-10-05 23:01 ===
* Id: 97F9521
* User: SoWhy
* Date: 2018-09-12 07:46:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|859178530|STYLE 859178530}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|859178531|POLICY 859178531}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|859178533|PROJ 859178533}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|862675381|STYLE 862675381}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|862675384|POLICY 862675384}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/WikiProjects_and_collaborations|prev|862675386|PROJ 862675386}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
The guideline '''currently contains the following wording''':

{{talkquote|The point of these template boxes is not to list every single redirect for any given page (indeed, that's what [[Special:WhatLinksHere]] is for); instead, they generally should list only one or two common and easily remembered redirects.}}

This guideline has been largely ignored by the community for almost ten years and for good reasons, so I changed this to 

{{talkquote|The point of these template boxes is not to list every single redirect for any given page (indeed, that's what [[Special:WhatLinksHere]] is for); instead, they generally should list <del>only one or two</del> <ins>the most</ins> common and easily remembered redirects.}}

but was reverted.

I thus formerly '''propose this change be implemented''' as it reflects standard and current practice as evidenced by [[WP:V]], [[WP:NOT]], [[WP:DEL]], [[WP:EP]] and [[WP:NPOV]] to name but a few core policy pages. While listing all possible shortcuts is overkill, it's also [[WP:COMMONSENSE]] that there should not be an artificial limit. If a page has four common shortcuts, they should be listed and if it only has one, so be it. Removing shortcuts solely for the sake of removing a certain number strikes me as [[WP:BURO|following the letter of the rules for the sake of following the rules without thought of whether doing so really improves the project]] (something, ironically, I have been accused of in the past).

'''This RFC is ''only'' about whether the wording should be changed from "only one or two" to "the most". '''

Pinging editors who were involved in removing shortcuts: {{u|Johnuniq}}, {{u|Carl Tristan Orense}}, {{u|Galobtter}}, {{u|Izno}}.

Regards [[User:SoWhy|<span style="color:#7A2F2F;font-variant:small-caps">So</span>]][[User talk:SoWhy|<span style="color:#474F84;font-variant:small-caps">Why</span>]] 07:46, 12 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject UK geography/How to write about counties#rfc_D52E474|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject UK geography/How to write about counties]] expired 2018-10-06 16:01 ===
* Id: D52E474
* User: Roger 8 Roger
* Date: 2018-10-04 08:56:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|862662360|UNSORTED 862662360}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/History_and_geography|prev|862724754|HIST 862724754}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|862724756|POL 862724756}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|862763655|POL 862763655}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Unsorted|prev|862771002|UNSORTED 862771002}}
* RFC Text:

The current guidelines were adopted around 15 years ago and have led to numerous editorial contradictions and circular discussions. This means the guidelines don't work properly and need updating. It is even questionable whether there ever has been a consensus created. I hope a healthy debate will follow here first. Many other editors who use the various county related sites should also be advised of this discussion, and someone might also begin a [[wp:RfC|Request for Comment]].

The current guidelines are factually incorrect in claiming the historic counties no longer exist. This is probably the route cause of most of the problem. The use of the word 'county' to refer to different things comes a close second. Change will not be easy because there are so many inter-connected articles and assumptions, but change is necessary. We must keep any changes simple and not get trapped into discussing the minutiae. However, precision is important, because the lack of it has led to the current muddle. I very much think we should avoid discussing at any length whether historic counties exist of not. Some people just don't get it so we are better off just accepting that and moving forward. I propose the following:

'''1/ When referring to a county, the default meaning is the traditional/historic county'''. Different meanings of any name are qualified by such words as Essex (Ceremonial county). It is more often than not that confusion arises by using the ceremonial county as the default, even though it was originally thought this would not be the case.

This means, for example, there will be an article named Essex dealing with the historic county and one called Essex (Ceremonial county) dealing with the more recent area. The current Essex article will not change much, and would have a small sub-section on recent local govt, referring to the CC article: the new article, Essex (CC) would deal only with that county, mainly local government. This is no different from countless other article topics.

'''2/  Have separate articles for the different types of county'''. Combining everything together is not practically possible without making [[wp:pov|POV]] assumptions that trigger the endless edit wars. Inserting opinions and false information not backed by the evidence or by closer examination does Wikipedia a dis-service.

'''3/  Use the term 'traditional' county (as does the govt), because 'historic' can be confusing.''' The use of the word historic has caused much of the misunderstanding that has created the confusion.

...If we adopt these two changes alone, there will be limited need to change the numerous contradictions in the articles because the changes once made will easily lead to the fairly quick ironing out by editors of so many problems caused by the current way of handling counties. There will be problems relating to each county but they will be reasonably easy to deal with once we have adopted point 1 above. [[User:Roger 8 Roger|Roger 8 Roger]] ([[User talk:Roger 8 Roger|talk]]) 08:56, 4 October 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Naming conventions (government and legislation)#rfc_C000AA9|Wikipedia talk:Naming conventions (government and legislation)]] expired 2018-10-06 21:01 ===
* Id: C000AA9
* User: Number 57
* Date: 2018-09-06 20:41:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|858391348|POL 858391348}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|865212240|STYLE 865212240}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Politics,_government,_and_law|prev|869637008|POL 869637008}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|869637012|STYLE 869637012}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
I'd like to propose amending our naming format for elections/referendums to move the year to the front of the title; so, for example, [[French presidential election, 2017]] would be [[2017 French presidential election]]. I think this has several advantages:
#It brings election articles in line with the vast majority of other articles with years in the title
#It allows the article titles to be used in prose, as the current format cannot be used (one could say "the [[2017 German federal election]] resulted in a hung parliament")
#It would make certain election articles titles more logical (for instance [[United States Senate election in Florida, 2018]] would become [[2018 United States Senate election in Florida]]
#It would make the titles of related articles more logical (for instance [[Fundraising in the United States presidential election, 2016]] would become [[Fundraising in the 2016 United States presidential election]])
#It would automatically sort elections by year in categories

I mentioned this a year ago at [[WP:E&R]] and a valid point was raised that currently you can start searching "French presidential election" and you get the whole list. This is an advantage, but as far as I can see, the only one. A way to keep this benefit is to still create redirects from these titles.

This will involve moving many thousands of articles (I will notify as many relevant WPs as I can find), so I propose that if this passes, a bot run is set up to do it. Cheers, [[User:Number 57|<span style="color: orange;">Number</span>]] [[User talk:Number 57|<span style="color: green;">5</span>]][[Special:Contributions/Number 57|<span style="color: blue;">7</span>]] 20:41, 6 September 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
Should we prevent new users from indexing pages in the user namespace?

Recently, a [[Special:AbuseFilter/930|new edit filter]] was created which disallowed new users indexing pages in userspace. The filter was later set to log because there wasn't a custom warning, and also there has not been consensus for disallowing userpage indexing by new users. Something like this was suggested in [[Wikipedia:Village pump (proposals)/Archive 151#Inform of noindexing before user page creation|the discussion of this (failed) proposal,]] so this proposal is to gather consensus on this. <span style="text-shadow:#069 0.2em 0.2em 0.5em; class=texhtml">[[User:SemiHypercube|<b style="color:#090"><sup>Semi</sup></b>]][[User talk:SemiHypercube|<b style="color:#099"><sub>Hypercube</sub></b>]] [[Special:Contributions/SemiHypercube|‚úé]]</span> 23:28, 24 September 2018 (UTC)}}

{{rfcquote|text=
<div id="rfctoc" class="toc" style="float:right">
{{center|'''Rfc options'''}}
{{blist |class="toc" |style=margin:0.3em 0.2em
  | ‚Ä¢ [[#Delete the entire BLP|Delete the entire BLP]]
  | ‚Ä¢ [[#Keep ROGD content in the BLP|Keep ROGD content in the BLP]]

At this time, I think the article is adequately [[WP:NPOV|NPOV]]-compliant on the topic of ROGD. However, it is clearly {{em|not}} NPOV-compliant on the topic of [[Lisa Littman]], the nominal subject of the page. It's still a [[WP:BLP|BLP]] that has instead become a [[WP:coatrack|coatrack]] for a [[WP:RECENT]] controversy, resulting in serious issues including [[WP:BALASP]].

Despite legitimate concerns about [[WP:RECENT|recentism]] and [[WP:NOTNEWS]], I think we have a consensus that the ROGD content of this article belongs in Wikipedia, {{em|somewhere}}. But there's no consensus about what action should be taken.

These are the possibilities that I see, and I'm inviting a discussion under each heading. <small><span style="color:#0;border:0;font-weight:normal;padding:0 1px 0 1px;text-shadow:1px 4px 8px #F70,-8px -6px 10px #ee7f2d,1px 1px 1px #FFF;">[[User:Lwarrenwiki|Lwarrenwiki]] ([[User talk:Lwarrenwiki|talk]])</span></small> 19:46, 7 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Articles for creation#rfc_0446967|Wikipedia talk:WikiProject Articles for creation]] expired 2018-10-10 07:01 ===
* Id: 0446967
* User: Enterprisey
* Date: 2018-09-10 06:09:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|858879142|PROP 858879142}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|863352120|PROP 863352120}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
This is a proposal to put all AfC status templates, maintenance templates, comments, and such on the draft talk page instead of the draft page, where they currently are. This would enable reviewers and draft authors to hold normal conversations on the talk page, and would (as a side effect) retain all conversation if the draft is moved to mainspace. A general disclaimer-style AfC banner will remain on the draft page, informing readers that the draft is not an article yet. A script (or Lua template) can also be written to summarize the status of the draft so far, for use by reviewers and others interested in AfC reviewing operations. Robert McClenon was the most recent person to suggest this, and this issue has also come up in the past before then. [[User:Enterprisey|Enterprisey]]&nbsp;([[User talk:Enterprisey|talk!]]) 06:09, 10 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Featured picture criteria#rfc_F183858|Wikipedia talk:Featured picture criteria]] expired 2018-10-12 04:01 ===
* Id: F183858
* User: Coffeeandcrumbs
* Date: 2018-09-12 03:42:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|860698293|PROP 860698293}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_proposals|prev|863655377|PROP 863655377}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
*The article in bold, featured along with the [[WP:Picture of the day|Picture of the day]], should meet the minimum quality standards for [[WP:V|verifiability]] as required by other sections of the [[Main Page]] like [[WP:OTD]], [[WP:DYK]], and [[WP:ITN]]. All content found in the blurb should be verifiable somewhere on Wikipedia, preferably the article in bold. If the blurb contains information not relevant to the article in bold but relevant to the image, that information should be verifiable in a citation contained in one of the articles linked in the blurb. ---&nbsp;[[User talk:Coffeeandcrumbs|<span style="color:#CC2200">Coffee</span>]]<nowiki/>and[[Special:Contributions/Coffeeandcrumbs|<span style="color:#663366">crumbs</span>]] 03:42, 12 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Here (Alicia Keys album)#rfc_CBDD97E|Talk:Here (Alicia Keys album)]] expired 2018-10-12 10:01 ===
* Id: CBDD97E
* User: Dan56
* Date: 2018-09-14 00:12:00

* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
In [[Here (Alicia Keys album)#Critical reception|the critical reception section]] the sentence, "''Here'' was met with generally positive reviews from critics", was given three citations--all to [[Wikipedia:Identifying_and_using_independent_sources#Non-independent_sources|press releases]]--by ''someone'' ([https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Here_%28Alicia_Keys_album%29&type=revision&diff=859324408&oldid=859245792]). The following sentence, mentioning Metacritic's aggregate score for this album, had a citation in place, to Metacritic, which itself says the album received "generally favorable reviews" ([https://www.metacritic.com/music/here/alicia-keys]). I reverted the addition of the three citations, regarding it as a case of [[WP:CITEOVERKILL|citation overkill]], before they were restored by ''someone'' ([https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Here_%28Alicia_Keys_album%29&type=revision&diff=859333965&oldid=859331873]). Should they be removed? [[User:Dan56|Dan56]] ([[User talk:Dan56|talk]]) 00:12, 14 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Tom Crean (explorer)#rfc_853CF7D|Talk:Tom Crean (explorer)]] expired 2018-10-12 12:01 ===
* Id: 853CF7D
* User: Spintendo
* Date: 2018-09-27 06:48:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|861722528|BIO 861722528}}

{{rfcquote|text=
* {{cite book |last1=Foley |first1=Tim |title=Crean: The Extraordinary Life of an Irish Hero |date=2018 |publisher=Keel Foley Publishing}}
* {{isbn|978-1-9999189-1-0}}
* {{asin|1999918932}}

The writer of the above <u>self-published book</u> (editor {{u|Timfoley50}}) has asked to incorporate changes <u>from their book</u> into the article. These changes include:
# Three changes to ''Early life and career''
# Six changes to ''Later life'' section
# Four changes to ''Imperial Trans-Antarctic Expedition'' section
# One change to ''Terra Nova expedition'' section
# Three changes to ''Legacy'' section
# Three changes to ''Notes'' section
# Two changes to ''External links'' section

I've already taken the request to the [[Wikipedia:Reliable_sources/Noticeboard|reliable sources noticeboard]], where the response was that the request was too lengthy and/or too technical. However, nothing was stated at that time about the ''reliability'' of the source. Editors here are asked to comment on the suitability and feasibility of incorporating these edits into the article. Below in the collapsible section are his requested changes. Please note that in instances where the text refers to "I" or "My" or "Me", this is referring to the COI editor {{u|Timfoley50}} and not myself, Spintendo. I have copied the text in the collapsible section from an earlier post made by the COI editor on this talk page in their initial COI edit request which I answered. Based on the COI editor's feedback,  additional alterations to that quoted text were made, including the addition of a numbering system to the individual requests which was not present in the original COI edit request. The COI editor is monitoring this page and will answer any questions/concerns that other editors have. '''<span style="font-size:80%;border:2px solid #FB2B11;border-radius:50px;font-color:#00008b">[[User talk:Spintendo|<span style="color:#00008b;">&nbsp;Spintendo&nbsp;</span>]]</span>''' 06:48, 27 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)#rfc_2008C32|Wikipedia:Village pump (policy)]] expired 2018-10-14 03:01 ===
* Id: 2008C32
* User: Ivanvector
* Date: 2018-09-24 13:33:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|860998421|POLICY 860998421}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|865530908|POLICY 865530908}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
There is an issue currently with the [[Wikipedia:Proposed deletion|proposed deletion policy]] (PROD) which is causing some confusion and ambiguity. In January this year, user {{ul|Green Giant}} [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikipedia:Proposed_deletion&diff=next&oldid=823134643 boldly edited the policy] to simplify the wording, but in doing so, changed the ''suggestion'' to notify article creators to a ''requirement''. It appears as though this was not compelled by any discussion to make that change, and it was also certainly in good faith and possibly not intended to have changed the meaning in this way. Up until this change, our various deletion policies all suggested notifying article creators and significant contributors as a courtesy, but did not require it (and requiring AfD notification is a [[Wikipedia:Perennial proposals#All authors must be notified of deletion|perennial proposal]]). With Green Giant's change, PROD stands out as the only deletion process requiring notification. The change has also not been well publicized or recognized - this post is inspired by an editor reported to ANI for failing to notify, and several editors and administrators responding that they were not aware of the change.

I am proposing a <s>three-pronged</s> discussion/straw poll to determine the community's current opinions about proposed deletion. Please comment in one of the sections below. [[User:Ivanvector|Ivanvector]] (<sup>[[User talk:Ivanvector|Talk]]</sup>/<sub>[[Special:Contributions/Ivanvector|Edits]]</sub>) 13:33, 24 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Kind of Blue#rfc_1BE2783|Talk:Kind of Blue]] expired 2018-10-16 15:01 ===
* Id: 1BE2783
* User: Dan56
* Date: 2018-09-16 14:34:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|859827728|MEDIA 859827728}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|861892422|STYLE 861892422}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|864332190|MEDIA 864332190}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_style_and_naming|prev|864332191|STYLE 864332191}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Recently, the paragraphs in the lead were [https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kind_of_Blue&type=revision&diff=796808681&oldid=796668435 rearranged] by {{u|Lawrencekhoo}}, so that information about the album's release date, recording, and the musician's concept for the album were replaced in the first paragraph with information about how the album has been critically received, accolades, and so forth. Lawrencekhoo cited the guideline that the lead should establish notability of the topic. In restoring the original layout, I cited [[MOS:LEAD]] which says the lead paragraph "should establish the context in which the topic is being considered by supplying the set of circumstances or facts that surround it," and in my opinion, critical opinions are not facts. The practice throughout WP:ALBUMS articles appears to prioritize the original layout here, but admittedly my opinion is not a strong one when reading: "The notability of the article's subject is usually established in the first few sentences. Like in the body of the article itself, the emphasis given to material in the lead should roughly reflect its importance to the topic, according to reliable, published sources." So I'm not sure. [[User:Dan56|Dan56]] ([[User talk:Dan56|talk]]) 14:34, 16 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Talk:Dark wave#rfc_CC04A2E|Talk:Dark wave]] expired 2018-10-18 11:01 ===
* Id: CC04A2E
* User: Ilovetopaint
* Date: 2018-09-18 10:30:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|860104146|MEDIA 860104146}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Media,_the_arts,_and_architecture|prev|864613274|MEDIA 864613274}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Here are some claims taken from the article [[Dark wave]], followed by the cited text used to support that claim. Please pay '''close attention''' to the phrasing of the claim and the phrasing of the sources. Ask yourself, "are they 100% saying the same thing?"
{{talkquote|
{{div col}}
* '''Claim A:''' [[Coldwave]] is a subgenre of dark wave
*: '''Source:''' "{{tq|Dark Wave is a [...] generic term for dark varieties of the Wave, which also subsumes Gothic. Cold Wave is a subgenus of experimental, minimalist electronic music from France.}}" (translated from German)
* '''Claim B:''' Some instruments that are common to dark wave include guitar, bass guitar, drum machine, cello, piano, and samplers
*: '''Source:''' same as above
* '''Claim C:''' [[Neofolk]] is a subgenre of dark wave
*: '''Source:''' "{{tq|The dark wave scene is divided among other things in the classic dark wave, gothic rock, electronic groups or even the neofolk.}}" (translated from German)
* '''Claim D:''' Dark wave borrows elements from the [[post-industrial]] genre.
*: '''Source:''' "{{tq|At first, there wasn't the same sort of [Goth] scene and we were in more of an '[[industrial music|industrial]]' thing. There was nothing like the clubs you get now [...] it's not just Goth, it's a mix - Darkwave or whatever.}}" [http://sortedmagazine.com/archive/magazine/sordid/attrition.htm]
*  '''Claim E''': Gary Numan and Depeche Mode were associated with gothic rock and synthesizer-based new wave music
*: '''Source:''' "{{tq|The term "darkwave" came from back in the 1980s, and was one of the terms used to describe [the] Golden Age [of gothic rock] bands, as well as dark electronica acts like Gary Numan and Depeche Mode.}}" [http://www.houstonpress.com/music/the-seven-ages-of-goth-6500894]
{{div col end}}
}}
Based on these examples, is it reasonable to suggest that the article possibly contains [[WP:SYNTH|synthesized claims]], or [[WP:STICKTOSOURCE|claims that are not supported by the sources]]?
--[[User:Ilovetopaint|Ilovetopaint]] ([[User talk:Ilovetopaint|talk]]) 10:30, 18 September 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Identifying reliable sources#rfc_85F04FE|Wikipedia talk:Identifying reliable sources]] expired 2018-10-20 08:01 ===
* Id: 85F04FE
* User: Newslinger#top
* Date: 2018-10-19 18:32:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|864829281|POLICY 864829281}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|864899446|POLICY 864899446}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Should the following section be included in {{sectionlink|Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources|Questionable sources}}?
{{tq2|

''' Web content by non-staff contributors '''

{{Shortcut|WP:CONTRIBUTOR|WP:CONTRIBUTORS}}
On [[Online newspaper|news websites]], [[periodical]] websites (excluding [[academic journals]]), and [[blog]]s, [[web content]] authored by non-staff [[Freelancer|contributors]] is questionable, even if it is published in a source that is otherwise reliable. Compared to [[staff writer]]s, contributors are subject to reduced editorial oversight and have a lesser reputation for fact-checking and error correction. Reliable publications distinguish articles written by staff writers from ones written by contributors by indicating the author's job title in the [[byline]]. Less reputable sources only display the author's job title on their profile page or the website's [[Masthead (publishing)|masthead]].

Examples of sources that publish content from non-staff contributors include [[WP:RSP#Forbes.com contributors|Forbes.com]] and ''[[WP:RSP#HuffPost contributors|HuffPost]]''.

[[Opinion piece]]s in reliable sources have their [[#Statements of opinion|own guideline]], which applies in addition to this one.
}}
‚Äî&nbsp;'''''[[User:Newslinger|<span style="color:#536267;">Newslinger</span>]]'''&nbsp;<small>[[User talk:Newslinger#top|<span style="color:#708090;">talk</span>]]</small>'' 18:32, 19 October 2018 (UTC)}}

=== [[Wikipedia talk:Biographies of living persons#rfc_8186A8C|Wikipedia talk:Biographies of living persons]] expired 2018-10-21 01:01 ===
* Id: 8186A8C
* User: Jytdog
* Date: 2018-10-09 15:32:00
* Revisions affecting this RFC:
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|863271417|BIO 863271417}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|863515802|POLICY 863515802}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Biographies|prev|864999860|BIO 864999860}}
** {{Diff|Wikipedia:Requests_for_comment/Wikipedia_policies_and_guidelines|prev|864999867|POLICY 864999867}}
* RFC Text:

{{rfcquote|text=
Should any of the following be added at the end of the [[WP:BLPSPS]] subsection?

*1) However, if a living person promotes pseudoscience or fringe theories, or has published work that is inconsistent with accepted scientific or scholarly methods, the [[WP:PSCI]] policy and [[WP:FRINGE]] guideline come into play with respect to that theories or work. Content ''about'' that person's theories or work may be sourced to high quality expert third party SPS per [[WP:PARITY]]; such sources may only be used to generate content about the theory or work, not the person.{{efn|As examples only, commonly used sources for this purpose include ''[[Retraction Watch]]'', ''[[Science-Based Medicine]]'', and ''[[Quackwatch]]''}}</blockquote>

*1a) Same as 1), but including at the end: "Content generated using such sources should be attributed if it goes beyond simple facts" {{efn|"simple facts" are "X's medical license was revoked by Y on Z date." or "Paper A was retracted by journal B for given reason C"}}

*1b)  Same as 1), but including at the end: "Content generated using such sources should be attributed."
{{notelist-talk}}
-- [[User:Jytdog|Jytdog]] ([[User talk:Jytdog|talk]]) 15:32, 9 October 2018 (UTC)}}
